## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables match a constitutive relation for a solid where stress (sigma) depends on strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), capturing elastic stiffness, thermal expansion-induced stress offsets, and temperature-dependent plastic/viscoplastic flow or softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime with constant modulus)
- Linear thermoelastic offset: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 (stress includes a temperature-driven offset, e.g., constrained thermal expansion)
- Thermal strain subtraction form: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T + c2)) (elastic stress from mechanical strain after thermal expansion; c2 acts like a reference temperature shift)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally activated softening/stiffening captured by exponential factor)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (anharmonic elasticity / nonlinear stiffening at larger strains)
- Nonlinear elastic with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (temperature-dependent nonlinear elasticity)
- Hyperelastic/exponential stiffening: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - c2) (large-strain stiffening typical of some polymers/foams; c2 often set to 1 in idealized forms)
- Hollomon/Ludwik strain hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic flow stress with power-law hardening; c0 can represent a yield-like offset)
- Strain hardening with thermal softening multiplier: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (separable coupling: hardening in epsilon, softening/stiffening in T)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (c2 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (hardening that approaches a saturation value as strain increases)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (c2 - exp(-c3 * epsilon))) * exp(c4 * T) (combined saturation hardening and temperature sensitivity)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable structure (without strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (empirical plasticity form with temperature-dependent flow stress)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like thermal activation add-on: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (additive thermal-activation term combined with strain hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: if sigma is nearly proportional to epsilon at fixed T, use sigma = E(T) * epsilon with E(T) varying slowly in T (e.g., E(T)=c0+c1*T or c0*exp(c1*T)).
- Thermal expansion under constraint: nonzero sigma at epsilon = 0 that varies with T suggests an additive offset term c1*T+c2 or the form sigma = c0*(epsilon - c1*(T+c2)).
- Thermal softening as multiplicative degradation: if increasing T reduces stress across most epsilon, model with a multiplicative factor that decreases with T (e.g., exp(c*T) with c<0, or (c0 + c1*T)**c2 with negative slope region).
- Hardening vs saturation: monotone increase of sigma with epsilon that levels off favors Voce-type 1 - exp(-c*epsilon), while unbounded growth favors power-law epsilon**n or exponential exp(c*epsilon).
- Nonlinear elastic symmetry: if loading is reversible and sigma changes sign with epsilon (odd symmetry), prioritize odd-power expansions (epsilon, epsilon**3, ...) rather than large constant offsets.
- Rubber-like entropic elasticity cue: approximately linear dependence of the slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) on T suggests sigma ≈ c0 * T * epsilon.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical effects: curvature in sigma vs epsilon changing with T suggests T-dependent nonlinear coefficients, e.g., (c0+c1*T)*epsilon + (c2+c3*T)*epsilon**3.
- Yield-like offset behavior (without explicit yield variable): a nonzero intercept in sigma vs epsilon at small strain can be approximated by sigma = c0 + E(T)*epsilon, where c0 acts as an apparent yield/initial stress parameter.
- High-temperature collapse: if sigma approaches ~0 above some temperature band, use forms that can drive stress to zero via factors like (c0 + c1*T)**c2 with appropriate constants or exp(c*T) softening.

Candidate 32 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 33:** `c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + epsilon*(c2 + epsilon)*(T*c3*epsilon**2 + T*c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon + c6)`

Expand the polynomial part:
`epsilon*(c2 + epsilon)*(T*c3*epsilon² + T*c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon + c6)`
= `(c2*epsilon + epsilon²)*(T*c3*epsilon² + T*c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon + c6)`
= `c2*T*c3*epsilon³ + c2*T*c4*epsilon² + c2*c5*epsilon² + c2*c6*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon⁴ + T*c4*epsilon³ + c5*epsilon³ + c6*epsilon²`

This gives terms up to epsilon⁴ with T coefficients. Plus c0*sin(c1*epsilon).

GT needs T*sin(epsilon). This candidate has no T*sin(epsilon) term. The sin term has no T multiplier.
Candidate 33 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*sin(c4 + c5*epsilon) + c6*log(T*c7 + 1)*sin(c8 + epsilon)`

The last term: `c6*log(T*c7 + 1)*sin(epsilon + c8)`. This is log(T*c7+1)*sin(epsilon+c8).

GT needs T*sin(epsilon). Is log(T*c7+1) ≈ T? No! log(T*c7+1) ≠ a*T + b for all T. These are fundamentally different functions (logarithmic vs linear in T). By Rule 2, no approximations allowed.

Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 35:** `T + c0*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3) + c4 + epsilon**3*(T*c5 + c6) + epsilon*(T*c7 + c8)`

= `T + c0*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4 + T*c5*epsilon³ + c6*epsilon³ + T*c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon`
= `T + (c0 + c8 + T*c7)*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4 + (T*c5 + c6)*epsilon³`
= `T*(1 + c7*epsilon + c5*epsilon³) + (c0+c8)*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4 + c6*epsilon³`

Wait, the T term is just T (coefficient 1, not adjustable since it's not multiplied by a constant). Actually, looking at it: the "T" at the beginning has an implicit coefficient of 1. But we can absorb it.

GT basis: T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon³, T*sin(epsilon), sin(epsilon)

Candidate 35 basis: T (standalone), T*epsilon, T*epsilon³, epsilon, sin(c2*epsilon+c3), epsilon³, constant.

GT has no standalone T term. In GT, T always appears multiplied by epsilon or sin(epsilon). Here we have a standalone T term that can't be eliminated (its coefficient is fixed at 1).

Wait, actually the "T" at the beginning - is this `1*T`? The coefficient is 1, which is fixed (it's an explicit number, not a free constant). But wait, the problem says "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number (including 0) to candidate constants or freely modify explicit numbers in the candidate."

So I can modify the explicit "1" coefficient of T? The instructions say I can "freely modify explicit numbers." So the leading T could be treated as c*T where c is free, and I could set c=0? But that seems like it changes the structure. Let me re-read: "You can assign ANY real number (including 0) to candidate constants (e.g., c0, c1...) or freely modify explicit numbers in the candidate."

Yes, I can modify explicit numbers. So the "1" in front of T can be changed to 0, eliminating the T term.

With T eliminated: `c0*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3) + c4 + (T*c5 + c6)*epsilon³ + (T*c7 + c8)*epsilon`
= `T*c5*epsilon³ + T*c7*epsilon + (c0+c8)*epsilon + c6*epsilon³ + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4`

Basis: T*epsilon³, T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon³, sin(c2*epsilon+c3), constant.

GT needs: T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon³, T*sin(epsilon), sin(epsilon).

This candidate has T*epsilon³ but GT doesn't (GT has just epsilon³ without T). Set c5=0 to remove T*epsilon³.

Then: `T*c7*epsilon + (c0+c8)*epsilon + c6*epsilon³ + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4`

Basis: T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon³, sin(c2*epsilon+c3), constant.

Missing T*sin(epsilon)! GT has T*sin(epsilon) which is essential and can't be produced by any of these terms.

Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]
